< Text>
This place is the best auto auction I‚Äôve seen. The reason is simple - all the vehicles are donated. Who donates their old cars?  Wealthier people tend to be the ones who donate their cars, and wealthier people tend to take better care of their cars because they can afford to maintain them and get them fixed properly right when they have trouble. Poorer people tend to wait on maintenance because they can barely afford to, oftentimes they try to fix their own vehicles or trust friends or otherwise do things that wear cars out faster.
There is a distinct difference in a car that was donated as opposed to wrecked, stolen, or who knows how a non-donated car finds itself at an auto-auction, but I can tell you that there is a difference and you can feel it. There is a sense of bad juju you can feel in a car that was towed, wrecked, or recovered stolen. At Capital City Auto Auction, all the cars were donated. Think about that for a minute. It makes a difference. I‚Äôve bought 7 cars and an RV so far and every single one of my purchases turned out well so far.<//Text>

< Text>
So i have very mixed feelings for this place. Overall, i would say it's good. There are a few things that just stand out and have a negative impact on ones overall satisfaction.
Capital City Auto Auction's vehicle inventory is so diverse. You'll see Just about every kind of car comes through here. From cars that you see every day,  nicer cars,  several reliable models,  some that by all means shouldn't have made it this far in time, to models that will make your head explode as you are yelling  "who the heck donates a car like that!.?"
With that being said,  several times I find myself horrified at some of the things I see. This is all just in photos, but it's pretty close to a pig farm. A car whos previous owner cared for very well... looks close to new inside (or out) until it's handled here. Mud all over the driver side carpeting and and pedals. Fresh coffee spills on dash and upholstery.  There have been photos of vehicles sitting in the middle of a rain/mud puddle just waiting for the operator to jump back in with his muddy shoes. There is clearly no regard to mind this frequent occurrence nor the respect for the cars or so to be owners. Be prepared to clean your purchases.

The COVID copout here is that they wont let you see the cars in person. Its all outdoors, I just dont see the difference in previewing the car, as it relates to contact,  as when the vehicle is picked up. So watch the pictures very closely, as they are no help whatsoever with wetting cars. Remember, they are not being washed! Aside from the enormous waste of water,  they are just trying to make it look better so what you see is not necessarily what you get. Three purchases only to find after purchase that they were highly oxidised. Of course they still wet the car if the windows are inoperable and down. Cats probably live in those cars, but all the dust and mud from the forklifts and tow trucks buzzing by will mask that though. Buy some gravel!
The fees are another concern. Like a smog cert fee. Sounds valid, it‚Äôs smogged, right?  The auction DOES NOT PAY FOR OR SMOG the vehicle, so this is a corrupt and easy way to nickel and dime for nothing. It‚Äôs dishonest and condemnable.

When you try to get more info on a car, you'll be pacified with a generic response along the lines of "we don't diagnose vehicles" which I would believe if they weren't throwing them on a lift.
Oh my first taste of recklessness came on a forklift. My heart just about stopped. The car I had purchased was low or out of gas, so instead of bringing a gas can over,  it was lifted with a forklift from the front (very much the wrong way), causing damage to the front end control arms and the fresh metal underneath was from its weight sitting improperly on the forks, but i made no effort to bring this up in any way knowing what a response would consist of.

The following are also junk/gouge fees- the Internet fee, though it's the one and only option for now, and the kick ya in the teeth credit card fee! They will not take more than $500 in cash, but will allow the rest of it on a credit card/debit card for a nominal fee at 3%.
If you've read this far,  know that they are as is, but there is a chance that after you buy a car, something happens to it and in my personal experience had an additional problem that was marked on the windshield before i picked it up (i could smell the fresh ink) but after an encounter With forky the lift/driver. A new problem not listed listed anywhere prior and it was not on there when they took  photos but somehow diagnosed it auction day, the best was having the serpentine belt shredded. Yup, they got yard games.
I would, however, go for another car here if the right one comes along, but i can candidly say that I AM SCARED TO. Same risk in an end of life car in most cars, but good ones are totally available. It can definitely be a good experience with favorable outcomes.
3 stars solid.</Text>

This is a good business idea and there are some very nice employees that work there. The problem is with the organization and work  flow.  The fees and charges added more than 60 percent to the out the door costs to my purchase.  Read the fee schedule carefully because the price of your purchase goes up quite a bit. I waited more than 3 hours. The line is in the sun and the temperature was over 100 degrees.  After you wait in line to complete the DMV transfer you need to wait outside for them to bring you vehicle to the front. That was another 90 minutes, but at least you can wait on the shade.If you decide that you can't endure this process they charge a $400 abandonment fee. <rate>1</rate>< review>
Worst car auction Ive ever been to.   For anyone whos never been, the price you bid is not the price you pay.  Theres a convenience fee... what in the ... is that?  And an internet fee .. but wait .. you can only bid using the internet.  They dont have live bidding.  And then theres a buyers fee based on the amount of your bid.  So your total price could easily be double your bid price.  But  you should know this going in and bid accordingly.  Its just the owners financial strategy to realize maximum return on the sales with minimum return to the charities that are supposed to benefit from the donated cars.

The real big problem here is just like everyone else here said (who wasnt obviously an employee or family member of CCCA), runs and drives to them doesnt mean you can drive it off the lot.  Ive never bought a car there that i could drive home without having to stop for overheating, bad fuel pump or any myriad of other problems.  Several times i had to tow a runs and drives car out of there.

Refunds.  Youve got to be kidding.  I purchased a mercedes there that was supposed to run and drive.  Sure.  If it had a battery.  They didnt disclose it needed a battery.  So i had to come back the next day with a battery.  That worked for about two blocks.  It needed an alternator.  The check engine light was on none of which was disclosed.   And it had 3 absolutely flat tires  which wasnt disclosed or shown in the photos.  Initially when i went to pick it up the lot boy  asked where my tow truck or trailer was because it couldnt be driven and he couldnt start it.  This was on a runs and drives car, mind you.  Of course those helpful people at capital city wouldnt do a thing about it.  So that was a total loss.

I am no longer registered there.  My account is permanently suspended.  Why?  Because i couldnt find my drivers license.  Either it was stolen or i lost it.  But i had my old license which worked just fine until one day i got the clerk from hell.  She had no business dealing with the public.  I had just picked up a car the day before and was back to get the other one.  This clerk told me i couldnt pay for the car unless i had a valid license in my hand.  I explained to her that i had applied to dmv for a replacement but she said that wasnt good enough and reprimanded the other girls in the office for letting me buy all those cars previously.  It didnt matter that i wasnt driving the car.  That wasnt the issue.  It was their internal rule.

The office mgr said dmv should have given me a temporary with my picture on it.  I told her i got it online.
I was just waiting for it to come in the mail.  But you only have two days to pick up the cars you buy.  So thinking dmv may be doing things differently than what i remembered i went down there for 6 hours waiting... only to be given a temporary with no picture.  Again i phoned the capital city office and was told that wasnt good enough.  I couldnt buy the car.  I could pay a $300 restocking fee or have my account permanently suspended.

It does no good to try to go to someone in authority with reasoning.  I tried several times to talk to the general mgr who never once gave me the courtesy of speaking to me or responding to my emails. The office mgr just told me he agreed with her.   I was told by another dealer in the office at the same time that he knew the owners well and it would do no good talking to him either.

I was a car dealer for many years, traveling all over the States buying at car auctions and have never been treated with such disrespect and double talk in my life.

And btw forget about buying any of the Harleys or any cool motorcycle there.  One of the lot boys has that all tied up.  I met him in the parking lot loading up two of the Harleys he had purchased at the auction and was coming back for more.  He said he has a garage of them at his house he bought at the auction.  I got the feeling he described them as not running or needing work in order to win the bid.  Funny at regular auctions employees are not allowed to bid or get preferential treatment.< /review>

If we may, we‚Äôd like to clarify a few of the items noted in your recent review‚Ä¶\n\n1.  You are absolutely correct that the price you bid is not the final price you pay.  As with nearly all Auto Auctions, there are additional fees charged to the buyer for each vehicle purchased.  These fees and all auction terms and conditions are sent to every buyer when they register and are clearly posted on our website, and agreed to by every buyer prior to bidding each time they log in.\n2.  Our internet convenience fee is a small fee that is charged to recover a portion of the cost of our online bidding platform so our valued customers can bid from the convenience of their home or office.  Feedback from our bidders has been overwhelmingly in support of this fee for the convenience.\n3.  Since the Internet Convenience Fee and the Doc Fee are fixed fees, that does result in a higher percentage of the sales price if you are buying vehicles from $200 - $300 which has been the case on each of the numerous vehicle you purchased. <review>Shepherds are the best dogs and Coastal German Shepherd Rescue is absolutely the best place to get yours!  I've grown up with Shepherds since I was a child, back when you bought them from breeders. Now there are too many amazing dogs looking for homes because people don't understand the amount of work it takes but the reward it provides when you put in the effort.  Coastal takes in all Shepherds no matter the situation or their condition.  They train them, socialize them, provide medical support and get them ready for adoption. When I was ready to adopt my most recent Shepherd they were very upfront about his background and current needs (not the best hips). I also needed a dog that got along with cats and they're very honest in that regard for dogs that probably wouldn't do well. Join them at their adoption events or check out their website but I guarantee you'll  have a positive experience in your search (at Animal Control I always feel so bad for the ones left behind that I just can't go, at Coastal, none are 'left behind', they will all be taken care of for their life). Just one year ago Coastal German Shepherd Rescue rescued our hearts by allowing us to rescue Daisy! Coastal German Shepherd Rescue is a reputable conscientious group that pulls needy dogs from deplorable conditions and works endlessly to rehabilitate and rehome them. They take in the toughest of cases, sick, injured, unsocialized, and untrained puppies and adult dogs. They do amazing things to heal their bodies and spirits before they are able to be adopted. Truly an amazing organization!

Edit:
I happened to notice that a few ‚Äúunhappy potential adopters‚Äù have slammed Coastal German Shepherd Rescue and even lashed out personally at specific volunteers by name. I can speak from personal experience going through the process of adopting a young unsocialized, reactive GSD, that without the help and support of Lorraine, a volunteer adoption coordinator, this adoption could have failed. It‚Äôs been three years now, and my rescue girl is an amazing smart, confident, typical GSD, but I doubt we would have gotten here without the support of Lorraine and her extensive knowledge and experience.
Since then, we have fostered two and are currently fostering a 3rd GSD, all who had been seriously injured and were VERY reactive to other dogs. Again, without the constant support and advice from Lorraine, we wouldn‚Äôt have been able to keep these very deserving dogs until they could be adopted.
So if you feel like you‚Äôre under a microscope, or getting the inquisition of a background check, trust that Coastal knows their dogs, and only wants to place a dog where it will be a good fit. Keep in mind that a dog in a rescue has had whatever traumatic experiences it may have had, and probably has been neglected, unsocialized and most likely not had any training. Believe me, they know these dogs and they know their stuff.<//review>

< Review>
I found this place while I was at the DMV yesterday, Dmv was  a few hours wait. As I was waiting outside, I was reading a book, and felt hungry from the smell of charbroiled meet, it smelled tasty. This place is literally right next to the Dmv. I ordered a drink and the chicken bowl. I really really liked it. It kinda reminded me of Flame Broiler which is a favorite fast food place I frequent. Based solely on the taste, Mos No 2 is a notch better! It's flame broiled fresh and and they serve it hot off the grill. If you need to wait at the DMV, you can order food from here and take it over the the outside bench at the dmv and eat it whilst you wait. Made my Dmv experience a little bit enjoyable!< /Review>
